  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c50277a9-4373-4083-b866-3e1e718563d6'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText2427384192083418274" style="display:none">Sometimes, getting over pain and betrayal means Getting Up, Getting Even and Getting a Better Man.<br /><br />Astrid has planned out her perfect wedding. That is before she found out that her fiancé, Bryan, is cheating on her with her cousing-slash-best-friend-slash-maid-of-honor, Geena. And worse, Bryan got Geena pregnant.<br /><br />Just when Astrid thought it couldn’t get any worse, she received a wedding invitation telling her that her wedding will happen exactly the way she planned it. Except that she is no longer going to be the bride!<br /><br />So when her parents urged her to attend the wedding “as family”, she planned the perfect revenge. <br />She will put on a show for everyone to see. She’ll show them that she moved on with a better man—handsome, smart, rich and crazy about her.<br /><br />She’s even willing to pay a guy to be her “Knight in Shining Armani”.<br /><br />Then she met bartender, Ryder. Totally smoking hot and quite a charmer. Astrid thought he was perfect for the job.<br /><br />He pulled off the role quite well. Soon, her family thinks that Astrid was really with a smoking hot guy who wears Armani suits on a daily basis, drives a luxurious McLaren, and was totally in love with her.<br /><br />Astrid invented the perfect guy every girl would kill to date, and every ex-boyfriend would hate to be compared with.<br /><br />Or did she really just invent him?<br /><br />What if she really did kiss a frog, or tamed a beast?<br /><br />And that her quest for revenge was just the beginning of her happily ever after? <br /><br />=======<br /><br />Originally published on Wattpad in June 2013.<br /><br />Now available on <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.smashwords.com">www.smashwords.com</a><br /><br />and will soon be available in:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com">www.amazon.com</a></span>

<div id="review_827930361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827930361" />
    <a title="Justine Jaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27830001-justine-jaye"><img alt="Justine Jaye" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827930361?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine Jaye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine Jaye" href="/user/show/27830001-justine-jaye">Justine Jaye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827930361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16284037532356579514">I have read this book about a zillion times!<br/><br/>I disagree with the other review that this book was predictable, because it wasn't. Sure some parts of it were cliche, but there's always a twist, there was always something happening, just when you thought things were going smoothly!<br/><br/>True that the female character was frustrating at the beginning, but that is what made her unique from the other female leads. Then she got stronger and got over her inhibitions in the end. That's what a good chick literat</span>
  <span id="freeText16284037532356579514" style="display:none">I have read this book about a zillion times!<br /><br />I disagree with the other review that this book was predictable, because it wasn't. Sure some parts of it were cliche, but there's always a twist, there was always something happening, just when you thought things were going smoothly!<br /><br />True that the female character was frustrating at the beginning, but that is what made her unique from the other female leads. Then she got stronger and got over her inhibitions in the end. That's what a good chick literature is about.<br /><br />Ryder is really a Prince Charming in real life! I fell in love with him during the first chapters.<br /><br />I was hooked by this novel from the very beginning. The writing style is wonderful! The author has a gift to make you feel like you were in the shoes of the characters. I laughed with them, I cried with them. I felt all sorts of emotions when reading this book! Even anger and frustration. The author is THAT good!<br /><br />This is a modern day fairy tale that would make you believe in love and fairy tales again.<br /><br />This story does not just deserve to be read. It deserves to be read over and over again!<br /><br />It was worth every second of my time. It was indeed a wonderful journey, and a satisfying rollercoaster ride!<br /><br />I would recommend it to every sucker for romance reader out there!<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16284037532356579514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2966338397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2966338397" />
    <a title="Vintage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27204643-vintage"><img alt="Vintage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475253836p2/27204643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2966338397?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vintage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vintage" href="/user/show/27204643-vintage">Vintage</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=amnesia">amnesia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=bamboozled-hero">bamboozled-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=deception">deception</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=duped-heroine">duped-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=what-a-bitch">what-a-bitch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=apply-two-by-four-please">apply-two-by-four-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=nice-guy">nice-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=in-over-his-head">in-over-his-head</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27204643-vintage?shelf=poorly-written">poorly-written</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2966338397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2851150914192086116">I’m really conflicted as I feel I have been overly critical too many times, but this just had too much going on, like Certs, it was two mints in one. Or three.<br/><br/>Editor! Stat.<br/><br/>Plot 1: Trope of cheating fiancee, deceitful relative and martyr heroine<br/><br/>The heroine (who vacillates between being a blithering doormat and a whiny, time sucking crybaby) has just had her wedding hijacked by her cheating fiancee and her cousin who was like a sister, obviously a very bad sister. The book starts out promising and</span>
  <span id="freeText2851150914192086116" style="display:none">I’m really conflicted as I feel I have been overly critical too many times, but this just had too much going on, like Certs, it was two mints in one. Or three.<br /><br />Editor! Stat.<br /><br />Plot 1: Trope of cheating fiancee, deceitful relative and martyr heroine<br /><br />The heroine (who vacillates between being a blithering doormat and a whiny, time sucking crybaby) has just had her wedding hijacked by her cheating fiancee and her cousin who was like a sister, obviously a very bad sister. The book starts out promising and amusing as the now cynical heroine who no longer believes in “ever afters” is sabotaging the wedding ideas of a young bride. No green as it will make everyone think of vomit, and tulips are out because of a horror story where a dead bride is laid out on some tulips or something like that. Turns out the heroine was a wedding planner, but now that the bubble has burst can’t help pointing out the pitfalls of marriage. She gets fired, and the heroine goes downhill from there. She whines and carries on with her long-suffering friends and Adam, a semi cousin whose related to the fiancee stealer. Adam is the lone voice of sanity and the only character that stays consistently interesting and is not on page off enough. He has some dramatic back story I want to read. He’s also kind of an asshole to the heroine.<br /><br />The H arrives and he’s another <i>On the day that you were born the angels got together and decided to create a dream come true so they sprinkled moon dust in your hair of gold and starlight in your eyes of blue.</i> He’s the book equivalent of a Disney Prince Charming and too good to be true. In order to hold up her head at her cousin’s wedding that <b>she has to go to</b> she needs a fake fiancee that is educated, wealthy and charming because she never dates wealthy men. Ever. Wealthy men are the devil and will betray you every time. She adores her middle class orthodontist ex despite the fact he cheated on her with basically her sister. So who does does she meet? A <s>wealthy</s> charming bartender who promises he’ll be there as her date for $10,000. He shows up in an Armani suit, driving a McLaren and a Harry Winston 2 carat ring in his pocket. After an epic night where she can hold her head up again and loses her virginity, the H hands her the money back. The shoe hasn’t dropped yet and we’re not even at the 30% mark.<br /><br />She finally figures out who he is, but there’s more whining because he duped her. He’s not a poor bartender, but is really a wealthy man and she never dates wealthy men because blah blah.....<br /><br />Plot 2: Besotted hero chases reluctant heroine<br />Plot 3: Amnesia and love’s betrayal<br /><br />From here we have<br /><br />1. The H sweetly and romantically stalks her and charms everyone in her friends and family circle.<br /><br />2. Dupes her again by being her silent partner, a really silent and secret partner, so she can start her own wedding planning business. The cad.<br /><br />3. Finally gets her in bed again, but she’s still concerned about his money in that he has some.<br /><br />4. The H gets in a crash and gets amnesia, retrograde amnesia with the h the only one he can’t remember.<br /><br />5. Prince Charming turns into Dr. Evil and accuses the heroine of being a mercenary bitch where in his whole family wants to cap his ass but the heroine merely tears up in the corner. Again! Kleenex stock rises. His turnaround is utterly wrong and out of character for Little Mister Sunshine to morph into suspicious Greek tycoon behavior.<br /><br />6. He reneges on the business deal despite having a written contract. Is this possible?<br /><br />I think we were at the 60% point.<br /><br />Despite reader's exhaustion and whiplash, I finished. I still want Adam’s story, and this writer to get an editor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2851150914192086116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I need to read it </i> and yes one of the best chick books I have ever come across :D<br/><br/>Its starts as a predictable story but towards the end WOW it takes a huge turn :) <i> I ain't gonna spoil by writing more... so just read it </i><br/><br/>Lets start with RYDER :D (Where do you get such kinds of Disney kinda guy</span>
  <span id="freeText2817064055473083511" style="display:none">Can I just start by saying what an amazing book this has been *Swoony Eyes*<br><br>Just days back I have been reading books which are heavy on angst and I came across this book and I am like <i> Hey this sounds good... I need to read it </i> and yes one of the best chick books I have ever come across :D<br><br>Its starts as a predictable story but towards the end WOW it takes a huge turn :) <i> I ain't gonna spoil by writing more... so just read it </i><br><br>Lets start with RYDER :D (Where do you get such kinds of Disney kinda guy!!!)<br><br><a href="http://s1273.photobucket.com/user/m1990g/media/downloadSUIT_zpsdf31b34f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412324779i/11358682._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo downloadSUIT_zpsdf31b34f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ryder is one of the most charming persona I have ever read about *Grins* And Astrid ahhh she is lovely and sane and beautiful<br><br>Lets start with the story:<br><br>We are introduced to how Astrid is been cheated by her long time BF/Fiance with her own cousin and her cousin is now pregnant *_*<br><br>Well the thing is Astrid is a wedding planner, so when her wedding does not take place she turns a lil' bitter... she is sacked from her job and is now jobless. She stays with her half step bro Adam ( And might I say what a good cousin she has )<br><br>Now here is where the plot starts, as she gets an invitation to her Ex's wedding (YES!!! YES!!!) (Those suckers use her wedding for their own)<br><br>Now Astrid wants to rub it in her ex's and cousins face that all is well in Paradise. Her friends and Adam suggest that she hire a guy who will suit up in ARMANI and act rich, hot, Harvad educated and blah blah blah *Grins*<br><br>Enters swoony Ryder O_____O<br><br>He is a bartender (UMMMM!!! Ya lets go with that for now :P) who accepts Astrids plea to act as her Fiance (WOW!!!) Its hilarious :D<br><br>Not getting into much of what happens after this... I'd like to just point out some parts of the story which I really loved :D<br><br>The Ring that plays a very important part in the entire story:<br><br><a href="http://s1273.photobucket.com/user/m1990g/media/82cc981e050ca9bae51c98c8ded6c67e_zps06b5d510.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>The <b>
  <i> The EVER AFTER ... Malibu and Manhattan... Ryder helped Astrid in believing that she very much deserves an EVER AFTER *SWOOOOOOOON* </i>
</b><br><br> <a href="http://s1273.photobucket.com/user/m1990g/media/e4227174647ecccd09584ab128d15fe4_zps3786c07a.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <span id="freeText13960689458798924903" style="display:none"><b> "I realized that this is not a question of moral values. Love does get in the way of our principles and beliefs."<br /><br />-Astrid Jacobson </b><br /><br />(^__^(")<br /><br />+Enthralling, awesome, page-turner book!<br /><br />+As I told you before, in my other reviews that I'm not the kind of reader who's suckers for romance, BUT THIS!!!! THIS BOOK CHANGE IT. THIS IS EXCEPTIONAL! I can't even compare this to any other romance books that I've read. SURREAL! I still thought I was dreaming after reading this! OMG<br /><br />+Okay, let me give you some details about this lovely story. Not a MAJOR SPOILER. Because I want you to experience the thrill &amp; heart wrenching experience once you started reading this book. But I must warn you! I cried BUCKETS OF TEARS, I SOB! It's rare to find a book who can KEEP ME FROM CRYING ALMOST 10 MINUTES! DAMN! THIS IS DELICIOUSLY INSANE! LOL for the term! :)<br /><br />+I must warn you, if you continue to read this review I might spoil you a bit. Haha!<br /><br />+What I LOVE in this book:<br /><br />-MY DEAREST ADAM, he might be a little bit an ASS &amp; stubborn one, but I like how he sticks &amp; fight for ASH up until the end. He's a cocky gentle in the heart MONSTER. LOL! Love him! He's a book boyfriend! *blushing*<br /><br />-Ash FRIENDS, including Paris &amp; Ryder's mom. They are absolutely AWESOME! Specially Ash friends! They are the sweetest of all! TRUE FRIENDS STICK UP UNTIL THE END. They are the good example of that, after all everything ash been through. I like how the characters build there friendship. Soooo awesome!<br /><br />-ASTRID JACOBSON, the precious jem! Wow! Sometimes I hate her for being so stubborn annoying gal, but most of the time I loved &amp; admired her for being so strong! Lovely lady. :) Who deserves happiness.ü yayy! *KILEG*<br /><br />-MY RYDER VAN WOODSEN!!!! GOSH GOSH GOSH!!! He's A PERFECT BOOK BOYFRIEND! *screaminghisname* *giggling&amp;blushing* Yes. I LOVE HIM!!! I will stop spoiling just promise to read it!!!! I can't believe how the author put up a guy like him. He's too perfect to be true. I would like to meet him &amp; marry him. Lmao! Nah! Seriously, I love every little thing about him. Inside and outside! Haha!<br /><br />-Besides of the main characters, my favorite person in this story is ADAM. Amazing man. With a golden heart. Shhh... I admit I want more about him. I wish there was a story about him in other book that this author made. Haha I want to find out more.<br /><br />Sometimes I'm annoyed because of the main character, a little bit redundant. BUT the storyline is perfect, I don't have any IDEA how it will end. Gosh! I sob! Imagine that?! I rarely cry for books! At 3 am I was crying. Tears of sadness &amp; JOY! I must say that this would be my FIRST TEN STARS for the year 2016. (If they have options for that? LOL!)<br /><br />Friendship, loyalty, betrayal, relationship goals. Many more. I've learned many things. I'm so happy &amp; thankful. I owe this review to Nehjie Daylo who recommends this awesome book to me. Thank you for sharing! I'm looking forward to your reviews, soon here in GR! Please? :) lol!<br /><br />Miss Jerilee Kaye!!!!! ILOVEYOUSOMUCH!!! Kudos! I want to hug you right now! Thank you so much for sharing this fantastic story! I will definitely read all your books in the near future! :)<br /><br />Yes! Is it obvious?! I HIGHLY RECOMMEND THIS TO EVERYONE! THIS IS A MUST READ!!!! After reading this I believe in EVER AFTER! THEIR STORY MAKES ME BELIEVE THAT THERE IS FOREVER INDEED!<br /><br />You deserve to be happy TOO. READ IT NOW! ASAP!<br /><br />Fairytales do come true.ü<br /><br />^_^<br /><br />P.S<br /><br />Nehjie,<br />DAMN! I don't like to be a sweetysh*tfangirl! Haha! This all your fault!!! LOL! *HUGS*</span>

<div id="review_1593396041" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593396041" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20240026-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457018718p2/20240026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593396041?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/20240026-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20240026-emily?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593396041" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14369851110060419777"> First, let me preempt this with a few consolatory statements, to makes sure people don’t get too mad at me for this unpopular opinion about this book. I do not like giving out bad reviews to books, it makes me feel sad and I wonder what I missed from a book that other people loved. Also, I was really close to giving this book a 2, it was literally just the last 100 pages that made me really dislike the book and actually consider to just stop reading it. I like a good romantic chic lit book as m</span>
  <span id="freeText14369851110060419777" style="display:none"> First, let me preempt this with a few consolatory statements, to makes sure people don’t get too mad at me for this unpopular opinion about this book. I do not like giving out bad reviews to books, it makes me feel sad and I wonder what I missed from a book that other people loved. Also, I was really close to giving this book a 2, it was literally just the last 100 pages that made me really dislike the book and actually consider to just stop reading it. I like a good romantic chic lit book as much as the next person, and I don’t expect them to be these great pieces of work, but this book just had way too much for me to ignore. <br /><br />(1)	The first thing that really brought this story down for me from the very beginning was the writing style. For some reason for me the writing was flat and chunky, and really all of the dialogue felt very forced. Lines that were supposed to funny just didn’t really hit it for me, and the phrasing the author used was way too straight, there wasn’t really any colloquialism or anything to make the talking seem more natural. Also, sometimes the writing and phrasings the author used felt very British to me, especially with Ryders’s character and the way he spoke. This feeling was especially prevalent when he used the term of endearment ‘love’, I’m sorry but for me, American people cannot pull off that word. Maybe it was just a 'me' problem but I cringed every time he said it. <br /><br />(2)	The next biggest thing that threw me off was the main character, super annoying and whiney. Yes, I understand the fiancé leaving you for your cousin/ best friend is terrible, but there reaches a point when the friends should have stopped dealing with that whiney bullshit and slapped some sense into her. She was also crying ALL THE FUCKING TIME, and it was uncalled for, I understand once or twice, but it was like every chapter she had to cry about something. Another huge thing that bothered me was her problem with rich people, yes she had a bad experience with a high school boyfriend and feels she isn’t good enough that’s understandable, but not to the point where she is rejecting a man just because of the amount of money he makes. At no point does anybody of a higher class, like his friends or parents, say they disapprove of her because of her social class, but that one moment from high school has made her completely judgmental against the rich. It’s obnoxious and childish. <br /><br />(3)	My final thing with the story was how unrealistic it felt to me. Everything about just had me rolling my eyes and saying ‘yeah right’. I’m okay with cheesiness, especially with fluff, but there reaches a point where it passes cheesiness and just goes straight to the stupid, trope, soap opera scenario. Like the character Ryder, he was very unrealistic to me with the way he acted towards Astrid, especially the way he acted towards her after the car accident. Many of the scenarios I felt were put in there to just make the story longer and more dramatic, and that’s just not my thing. <br /><br /> So those are just condensed problems I had with the story (it seems long and I’m sorry, I’m the person that can go on long rants). For me as the story progressed, I just kept on getting more and more unsatisfied, and I feel like it could have been at the least 100 pages shorter, or, at least, things could have been taken out for better character development and building relationships. So that is my review on how I felt about the story, everybody has their own opinions so please don’t get too mad. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14369851110060419777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1190030980" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190030980" />
    <a title="Gobokairina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4205209-gobokairina"><img alt="Gobokairina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289182411p2/4205209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1190030980?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gobokairina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gobokairina" href="/user/show/4205209-gobokairina">Gobokairina</a>

  <span id="freeText18375301762271802133" style="display:none">3.5*<br /><br />But, I'm giving full marks for the sexy cover. <i>Phewitt...</i><br /><br /><u>Full review: 10/03/2015</u><br /><br />What will you do when your fiancé cheating on you with your cousin-best-friend-maid-of-honor? And, worse, your cousin is pregnant! <i>Perghhh</i>... it’s too much. <br /><br />This is what Astrid do -- planned the perfect revenge. She’ll show them that she moved on with a better man -- handsome, smart, rich and crazy about her.<br /><br />She met Ryder; a smoking hot bartender [?]. Astrid thought he was perfect for the job, and Ryder proved it right. He pulled off the role quite well. Soon, her family thinks that Astrid was really with a smoking hot guy who wears Armani suits on a daily basis, drives a luxurious McLaren, and was totally in love with her. But, what Astrid never thought that Ryder is not just a plain Ryder. Who he was, actually?<br /><br />I liked this story, but not giving full marks just because of that amnesia-thingy. <i>Sooo</i> melodrama. But it's ok, i’m still happy with the HEA. <i>Yay!</i><br /></span>

        <a title="moonlight ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="moonlight ☾" href="/user/show/37448930-moonlight">moonlight ☾</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3232429472&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3232429472" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1151870475021747080">✰ <b>5 stars</b> ✰<br/><br/>I loved everything about this book but the amnesia story line in the second half was meh. I have a love-hate relationship with that trope. Sometimes it works, sometimes it doesn't. It's all subjective at the end of the day and people may have liked the amnesia part but, for me, I found it cliche. :/ It's a good thing I loved the rest of this book (<i>especially the grovelling omg I live for a good grovel in romance books</i>) that I couldn't help but still rate it 5 stars, despite the trope.</span>
  <span id="freeText1151870475021747080" style="display:none">✰ <b>5 stars</b> ✰<br /><br />I loved everything about this book but the amnesia story line in the second half was meh. I have a love-hate relationship with that trope. Sometimes it works, sometimes it doesn't. It's all subjective at the end of the day and people may have liked the amnesia part but, for me, I found it cliche. :/ It's a good thing I loved the rest of this book (<i>especially the grovelling omg I live for a good grovel in romance books</i>) that I couldn't help but still rate it 5 stars, despite the trope.<br /><br />Ryder honestly stole my heart. The way he wouldn't give up pursuing Astrid, no matter how many times she wanted to stay just "friends" or keep up the fake act but not to the extent of making it real was swoon worthy. As for Astrid, I liked her, but she would annoy me sometimes. I understood where she was coming from with not wanting to get hurt again, but Ryder had already proven himself to be worthy so many times imo. Tho I truly felt for her in the scene when Ryder had amnesia and she had to put up with it. I wanted to hug her. :( Overall, I thought it was an enjoyable book! &lt;3</span>

  <span id="freeText8783817264765737271" style="display:none">I read this story at Wattpad and I literally stayed up until I read the last word. I cried, laughed, pulled my hair, hit my laptop a couple of times, got angry at Astrid for being so clueless (I love her to bits though) and swooned at Ryder. This book made me feel lots of feelings. I remember looking for a light summer read like a year or so ago and I stumbled at this and when I first finished it I was like whoa... And I was just in SHOCK on how good it was I head read it 2 times the next day and some more until the author took it down because it got published.<br /><br /> At first I was sad because I can't possibly buy this book because I thought my parents will freak out that I'm reading romance or whatever. Anyways, I still have to yet buy the book and I can't wait to get my hands on it...I've been thinking about this book a lot and I'll do whatever it takes to get this book in my hands. <br /><br />IF the author is reading this, I just want to say I love this story. <span id="freeTextContainer6070845070585544782"><strong>Grow up!</strong><br/><br/>I'm usually a non-violent person, but I wanted to smack the h so many times in this book. she creates and WHINES about drama when there is none and her friends enable it.   <span id="freeText6070845070585544782" style="display:none"><strong>Grow up!</strong><br /><br />I'm usually a non-violent person, but I wanted to smack the h so many times in this book. she creates and WHINES about drama when there is none and her friends enable it. Plus she is just too stupid to even function. Gee, I wonder if Ryder Van Woodsen could be the same as my Ryder Woodsen? <br /> The writing style seemed a bit basic; like this was how a 16 year old imagined adults dealing with adult problems. And it's really long and not in a good way. You know, you see a Kristen Ashley book and you know you're going to get a really fulfilling story- like a five course meal. You feel good after. I felt like I ate 5 courses of lettuce. I'm full, but it really doesn't feel all that good. <br />Carp, now in hungry. </span>

        <a title="Shantal  (VERIFED BOOK LOVER)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shantal  (VERIFED BOOK LOVER)" href="/user/show/7598301-shantal-verifed-book-lover">Shantal  (VERIFED BOOK LOVER)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2968829783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11286148411964556555">So I knew this book was going to be cliche because I read the synopsis but dang. To be fair I loved most things about this plot except I couldn't stand the heroine's indecision. It frankly drove me crazy and it really seemed like it dragged on just to make the book longer. It made no real sense in the plot even after the guy did every and anything to make her happy.<br/><br/>That was such a huge yawn.<br/><br/>Then when they did finally get together, the stupidest plot twist to have been invented went into this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText11286148411964556555" style="display:none">So I knew this book was going to be cliche because I read the synopsis but dang. To be fair I loved most things about this plot except I couldn't stand the heroine's indecision. It frankly drove me crazy and it really seemed like it dragged on just to make the book longer. It made no real sense in the plot even after the guy did every and anything to make her happy.<br /><br />That was such a huge yawn.<br /><br />Then when they did finally get together, the stupidest plot twist to have been invented went into this book. It reminded me of a cheesy soap opera. That particular introduction in the plot was not needed or warranted and it really only served to make this book that much longer. The complete 180 of the hero after this was even stupider. How can someone that was seemingly so sweet become so mean and crass suddenly. That just serves to show his personality with the heroine wasn't real. It really left a sour taste in my mouth and I really couldn't wrap my head around it.<br /><br />The last 1/4 of the book was very sweet but the plot twist threw everything off for me. Before, I would have given this a 4 stars just because despite it being cliche I still thought it was cute. The new direction just brought down my rating.<br /><br />3 stars .</span>
  <a data-text-id="11286148411964556555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText11401999326877683640" style="display:none">I finished this book in just two days after I read the book "intertwined" from the same author. <br /><br />I read these books after each other, and I must say I recognized a lot from both characters in each other. <br />This doesn't mean I didn't love both books, but if I have to choose I would recommend "intertwined" more, just because the emotions felt more real there. <br /><br />Nevertheless, the story was great, even as the characters playing their parts. <br />I loved their conversations and their humor. Some of the parts felt too long for me, and some parts were repetitive.       </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781494894351" href="/book/show/22052176-knight-in-shining-suit">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nandini by: </span>
      three of my usually non-reader friends
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1739375723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14383167451090704545"><b>3 more-or-less-average stars!</b><br/><br/>The break-down of <i>Knight in Shining Suit!</i><br/><br/><b>1. Why I decided to read the book:</b> It wasn't the dark, pretentious (though only slightly) cover that made me pick this book up which, if you see where I'm coming from, makes you presume a lot of things about the book, erotica/BDSM being on top of that list. However, what it clearly doesn't give off vibes of is <i>cute, fluffy, and ridiculously melodramatic</i> all of which it was. Anyway, the point here is, it wasn't any of those thi</span>
  <span id="freeText14383167451090704545" style="display:none"><b>3 more-or-less-average stars!</b><br /><br />The break-down of <i>Knight in Shining Suit!</i><br /><br /><b>1. Why I decided to read the book:</b> It wasn't the dark, pretentious (though only slightly) cover that made me pick this book up which, if you see where I'm coming from, makes you presume a lot of things about the book, erotica/BDSM being on top of that list. However, what it clearly doesn't give off vibes of is <i>cute, fluffy, and ridiculously melodramatic</i> all of which it was. Anyway, the point here is, it wasn't any of those things that made me want to read this book. Umm, no. It was a friend who isn't much of a reader but happens to be obsessed with this book. Now, the blurb wasn't entirely intriguing or anything, but since it was quite a persistent recommendation, I decided to give it a go. Plus, she even offered to lend me her copy, so I didn't have anything to lose here. And so that brings us to...<br /><br /><b>2. What this book lacked:</b> First off, this book definitely wasn't a quality read. The editing wasn't up to par, a lot of the dialogues of the later half of the book were just repetitions of the first half, the writing style was extremely amateurish, the characters had cookie-cutter personalities – the heartbroken, innocent girl, and the very rich, very famous, bad boy with a golden heart. It had all sorts of clichés thrown in, to a point that it was honestly too much. Moreover, it had a draggy plot with a little too much of the mainstream drama tropes like memory loss, accidents, a drunkard and jackass of an ex, yada yada.<br /><br /><b>3. What this book had:</b> Now, a lot of you might not know but I have a weakness for clichés. And this book was a breeding ground for exactly that. I'm not saying that I enjoyed the mixture of clichés (god, no, it really started getting very tiring) but they were enjoyable till a certain point! Ryder, our main guy made me roll my eyes once in a while with his overly grand gestures, but I still couldn't help but sort of fall in love with him too. I really liked the protagonist, Astrid, and loved the character development she went through during the entirety of the book. Adam was another character that I couldn't help but really like. Apart from that though, as I mentioned earlier, the drama was a bit over the top, but at the same time, it kept me wanting to read more to find out what happens next. (well, they're cliches for a reason, aren't they?)<br /><br />So despite its many flaws, this book was a fun read and I did enjoy reading it even if it got on my nerves a few times. I'd suggest it if you want something that's full of adorable cliches, has a mainstream stereotypical rich guy, and a book with a guaranteed happily ever after.<br /><br />P.S. Brownie points to whoever correctly guesses the number of times I've used the word <i>cliché</i> in this review! That's right, a lot of times!<br /><br />P.P.S. On second thoughts, this is a pretty contradictory review, non? Whoops, sorry!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14383167451090704545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1155413076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1155413076" />
    <a title="Romuelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28037510-romuelle"><img alt="Romuelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605758957p2/28037510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1155413076?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romuelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romuelle" href="/user/show/28037510-romuelle">Romuelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28037510-romuelle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155413076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14883048968366505423"><b>
  <i>Third time's the charm,</i>
</b> that's how it goes for some people (also for me!). Luckily, charm is present in this book from the first time I've read it to today's third time. I am just so glad that the feels are still in there. That even when I thought <i>Nah, I know this already</i>, it still managed to brought a lot of <i>awws</i> and a few tears out of me. I remember crying like a baby when I read this for the first time, though, and how I did not sleep that one Sunday because this book compelled me to fini</span>
  <span id="freeText14883048968366505423" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Third time's the charm,</i>
</b> that's how it goes for some people (also for me!). Luckily, charm is present in this book from the first time I've read it to today's third time. I am just so glad that the feels are still in there. That even when I thought <i>Nah, I know this already</i>, it still managed to brought a lot of <i>awws</i> and a few tears out of me. I remember crying like a baby when I read this for the first time, though, and how I did not sleep that one Sunday because this book compelled me to finish it.<br /><br /><p>
  <b>To be honest, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20257391.Knight_in_Shining_Suit" title="Knight in Shining Suit by Jerilee Kaye" rel="nofollow noopener"> Knight in Shining Suit</a> is far from perfect.</b>
</p><br />1. The writing style is not that impressive! Come on, who uses plenty of exclamation points?! <b>
  <i>"I'm on the edge, Astrid! Don't push me!"</i>
</b> Why on earth are these characters screaming? There are also a lot of misspelled words! The lead character's monologues are somewhat repetitive, too. (Hoped you see what I did there.) <br /><br /><p>2. <b>Astrid can be very annoying sometimes.</b> You will want to shake her from the inside out just so she can see what everybody else sees. She cries every minute as well. Is there something wrong with her tear ducts? But, okay, I do know some people who cries very easily and sometimes even without reason.</p><br />3. Ryder-after-Astrid is so dreamy, and cheesy. I've said before that I loathe cheesiness, so maybe Ryder is an exception. He's the type that most certainly does not exist in real life but you still wish <i>(oh so wish)</i> that he does. <br /><br /><p>4. There's a particular scene that got me shaking my head and saying "Very very wrong!" I don't need to have a background in medicine to know that when a person is injured, it's important not to move them until trained first-aiders come to their rescue. But hey, maybe it's just a minor injury and I'm only making irrelevant comments. </p><br />5. <b>The characters in this book are so melodramatic.</b> Reading this will make you feel like it's supposed to be a light book but is trying very hard to be dramatic at every turn. You know those kind that <b><u>always</u> happen in tv shows</b>? Get that? ALWAYS. <b>Always!</b> Need I say more? I guess not. But, you see, the cocaine used in cliché shows that makes them addictive is also sprinkled here. You'll be spellbound. <br /><br /><p>6. This is the kind of book that is far from reality. Probably. I can't imagine it happening in real life. <b>It's just a simple book, nothing extraordinary</b> to tell you the truth. However, KISS still screams "I'm a treasure" to me. <b><i>Huh, so biased!</i></b></p><br /><br />The flaws seems all clear to me now, and yet, I still loved the book!<br />So, yeah, <b>proceed at your own risk.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14883048968366505423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1374289948" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1374289948" />
    <a title="Ana Decosta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16194770-ana-decosta"><img alt="Ana Decosta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579251986p2/16194770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1374289948?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana Decosta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana Decosta" href="/user/show/16194770-ana-decosta">Ana Decosta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1374289948&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1374289948" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8812323745832494979">First of all, I wanted to say that anyone who got through the whole book deserves a golden freaking star! Three words : WAY. TOO. LONG. If you could cut all the crap out of it and get straight to the point it would be a bit more pleasant read.<br/><br/>I'm not really a fan of the heroine/I don't know what I want/damsel in distress/aka Astrid. I cannot even describe how infuriating she was at times with her indecisiveness and doubts, ARGGHH! I'm telling you - noooo man would give her a second thought after</span>
  <span id="freeText8812323745832494979" style="display:none">First of all, I wanted to say that anyone who got through the whole book deserves a golden freaking star! Three words : WAY. TOO. LONG. If you could cut all the crap out of it and get straight to the point it would be a bit more pleasant read.<br /><br />I'm not really a fan of the heroine/I don't know what I want/damsel in distress/aka Astrid. I cannot even describe how infuriating she was at times with her indecisiveness and doubts, ARGGHH! I'm telling you - noooo man would give her a second thought after a brush off she served Ryder with - multiple times! Which is my next point - guys like him do not exist. They're surreal. Like Taylor Swift's sense of humor or snow on a Hawaiian beach. <br /><br />About the lenght itself... seriously, why so much gabbing? It felt like all the were doing was talking about emotions, analysing feelings - repetitively. Less talking - more action! We don't need to know every single detail and thought going through that head of yours. Just as much as we don't need to read about EVERY DAMN KISS. I mean, come on! "He kissed me deeply" "He kissed me thoroughly" "He kissed me so sweet and long" etc etc etc... Yeah - we get it - you guys kissed. A LOT.<br /><br />Ryder didn't bother me that much (aside from being whipped), but Astrid was an overkill in everything she did. 1. Too naive - can't believe she did not ask/had no idea who the investor was when Adam told her about him.... it was just too obvious who it was. 2. Oblivious - when she found out Ryder didn't take the checks she gave him she never, not once, wondered - how could he afford the suit, the car AND the suite. Hah... brilliant.... 3. Too freaked out - About the 38743th time I read her saying "I'm not ready for a relationship and he's a very complicated man" I thought I was going to barf. What kind of complications did she have in mind?? He didn't have an ex wife he paid alimony for, he wasn't aggressive, he loved her deeply and he was faithful. Was money the complication? Oh, please... what a lame excuse. <br />It made my teeth hurt from all the sweetness they were surrounded with. All people told them how perfect they are together, how much they must love each other and how happy they look. Even Geena redeemed herself in a super long monologue that made me almost fall asleep.<br /><br />Thing with amnesia was too cliché , but then again, after all the reading I didn't expect anything original.... The story started good and at times I truly laughed but then I just weeped... Because I wanted this book to be something else... and it wasn't. Too bad. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8812323745832494979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YBFOx0fu+VGUn2MZ/9LOnX/mam1N1t1sefpsg7V3oXiiTSnwjrR+YSrgNJi0r86HnsMB571vhvhQpmIV619NAQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3j3NHa/H97lOpi4pm5A7NlUDazKZ+K1c20S8/L6NU+YcYaoqZp1wifDZeajQ7TsstCYAuGlB9sjyGLJq4KW/nw==')})
  }
